3.1 Assignation

Sometimes it will be useful to make a different data frame, and save it under a different name. In R, this is called an assigning an object to a variable, or an assignment. We do this by typing

new_object -< old_object

For example, the following command will create a new data set, called mycdc, that includes only the first 1000 rows if the original data set

mycdc <- head(cdc, 1000)

3.2 Ordering data by a variable

If we want to reorder the data according to the values of one of the columns, we can do that by using the command order( , ) the syntax is

data_frame[order(data_frame&variable), ]

Run the chinks of code below to see it in action

ordered <- cdc[order(mycdc$height), ]

Lets now see the first 10 rows of this new data set. Run the chunk of code below.

head(ordered, 10)
##       genhlth exerany hlthplan smoke100 height weight wtdesire age gender
## 732      good       1        1        0     53    130      115  29      f
## 303 very good       0        1        0     55     90       85  18      m
## 718 excellent       1        1        1     56    100      100  79      f
## 210      good       0        1        0     57    112      105  45      f
